## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and concentration A, which is a classic chemical kinetics problem. The rate law typically depends on the concentration raised to some power (reaction order), and may involve more complex mechanisms like reversible reactions or autocatalysis.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Zero-order rate law', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0', 'scenario': 'Reaction rate independent of concentration (e.g., surface-catalyzed reactions at saturation)'}
- {'name': 'First-order rate law', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to concentration (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)'}
- {'name': 'Second-order rate law', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to concentration squared (bimolecular reactions of same species)'}
- {'name': 'nth-order rate law', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1', 'scenario': 'General power-law kinetics with fractional or arbitrary reaction order'}
- {'name': 'Reversible first-order reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1', 'scenario': 'First-order forward reaction with reverse reaction approaching equilibrium'}
- {'name': 'Reversible reaction with equilibrium', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Combined first and second order kinetics, or parallel reaction pathways'}
- {'name': 'Autocatalytic reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)', 'scenario': 'Product catalyzes its own formation, logistic-type growth/decay in concentration'}
- {'name': 'Monod-type kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (A + c1)', 'scenario': 'Enzyme or microbial kinetics where rate saturates at high concentration'}
- {'name': 'Inhibition kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2)', 'scenario': 'Substrate inhibition where high concentrations reduce reaction rate'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent rate coefficient', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t)', 'scenario': 'Rate constant changes with time (e.g., temperature ramp, catalyst deactivation)'}
- {'name': 'Mixed-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A)', 'scenario': 'Transition between first-order (low A) and zero-order (high A) behavior'}
- {'name': 'Consecutive reaction intermediate', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t)', 'scenario': 'Concentration of intermediate species in consecutive A→B→C reactions'}
- {'name': 'Power-law with offset', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2', 'scenario': 'General rate law with constant production or consumption term'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate (consumption) → dA_dt typically has a negative coefficient multiplying A or A**n for reactant disappearance
- Reaction order identification → If log(|dA_dt|) vs log(A) is linear, the slope gives the reaction order n in rate = k*A**n
- Equilibrium approach → Rate law includes both negative and positive terms representing forward and reverse reactions, dA_dt → 0 at equilibrium
- Saturation in enzymatic systems → Rational form A/(A+c) transitions from linear to constant rate as A increases
- Autocatalytic signature → Rate has a maximum at intermediate concentrations, described by A*(c-A) type terms
- Consecutive mechanism fingerprint → Sum of exponentials in time indicates sequential reaction steps with distinct rate constants
- Half-life independence of concentration → Indicates first-order kinetics; half-life depending on initial concentration suggests higher order
- Conservation constraint → In closed systems, sum of concentrations is constant, allowing elimination of variables via c_total - A substitution
